The Intellect: Its Nature and Linguistic Origin
The author discusses the intellect's hidden nature and its linguistic derivation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the linguistic meaning of 'aql and why scholars caution against delving into its true nature.

Core Idea
The intellect is a hidden reality; its name comes from the idea of preventing deviation.

The author begins by comparing the intellect to the soul, noting that both are mysterious realities about which scholars differ on whether to investigate. He then provides the linguistic root of 'aql, which means 'to prevent' or 'to hobble,' indicating that the intellect restrains its possessor from error. This lesson explores these foundational insights.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the intellect's similarity to the soul
Pay attention to the author's comparison and his two differing opinions on investigating the intellect's reality.
2
Understand the linguistic definition
Note the root word and its implication: the intellect prevents one from straying.
3
Reflect on the caution
Why is it better to refrain from investigating hidden matters like the intellect? Consider the concept of al-mughayyabat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والعَقْلُ كَالرُّوحِ مبتدأ وخبر؛ أي: والعقل مثل الروح من حيث الخوض في بيان الحقيقة والوقف عن ذلك، واختلف كلام المصنف في الترجيح : فرجح في «هداية المريد» طريق الخوض، ورجّح في «الكبير» طريق الوقف، وهو المختار؛ لأنه من المغيبات، وكلُّ ما هو كذلك فالأولى الكف عن الخوض فيه.
لغة: وهو المنع، من (عَقَلَ البعير) : إذا منعه بالعِقال، وسُمِّي بذلك لمنعه صاحبه من العدول عن سواء السبيل.
واعلم أن العقل على خمسة أنواع :
الأول: غريزي؛ وهو غريزة يُتَهيَّأ بها لدرك العلوم النظرية، كما قاله الإسلام.
والثاني : كسبي؛ وهو ما يكتسبه الإنسان من معاشرة العقلاء.
والثالث : عطائي؛ وهو ما يعطيه الله للمؤمن؛ ليهتدوا به إلى الإيمان.
والرابع: عقل الزهاد؛ وهو الذي يكون به الزهد.
والخامس شرفي؛ وهو عقل نبينا ﷺ؛ لأنه أشرف العقول.
His statement: (And the intellect is like the soul) is a subject and predicate; that is, the intellect is like the soul in terms of delving into the clarification of reality and refraining from that. The author's statement differed regarding the preponderance: he gave preponderance in 'Hidayat al-Murid' to the way of delving, and gave preponderance in 'al-Kabir' to the way of refraining, and that is the chosen view because it is among the hidden matters, and everything that is like that, the better course is to refrain from delving into it.
Linguistically: it is prevention, from 'he hobbled the camel' when he prevented it with the hobble; it is so named because it prevents its possessor from deviating from the straight path.
And know that the intellect is of five types:
First: instinctive (gharizi); it is an instinct by which one is prepared to grasp theoretical sciences, as Islam stated.
Second: acquired (kasbi); it is what a person acquires from associating with rational people.
Third: granted (ata'i); it is what Allah gives to the believer so that they may be guided thereby to faith.
Fourth: the intellect of the ascetics; it is that by which asceticism is achieved.
Fifth: honorary (sharafi); it is the intellect of our Prophet ﷺ, because it is the most honorable of intellects.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification. It begins by explaining the line 'And the intellect is like the soul'—meaning they are similar regarding whether to investigate their reality or refrain. The commentator notes that the author himself gave two different preponderances: in his earlier work 'Hidayat al-Murid' he favored investigation, but in 'al-Kabir' he favored refraining, and the latter is chosen because the intellect (like the soul) pertains to hidden matters (al-mughayyabat), so it is better to avoid delving into it. Then a linguistic definition is given: 'aql derives from 'aqala al-ba'ir' (to hobble a camel), and is so called because it prevents its possessor from deviating from the straight path. Finally, five types of intellect are enumerated: instinctive (gharizi) enabling theoretical knowledge, acquired (kasbi) through association, granted (ata'i) by Allah to believers, the intellect of ascetics (zuhhad) enabling asceticism, and the honorary (sharafi) intellect of the Prophet Muhammad ﷺ, being the most honorable. Each type is briefly explained.

Key Terms
العقل (al-'aql)
عقال (al-'iqāl)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Both are physical entities
B) Both are hidden realities
C) Both are acquired
D) Both are instinctive

Key Takeaway
The intellect is a hidden reality that restrains its possessor from error, as indicated by its linguistic root.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Five Types of Intellect in Islamic Thought
The author enumerates five types of intellect with brief definitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list and explain the five types of intellect as enumerated by the author.

Core Idea
Intellect is not a single faculty; it appears as instinct, acquisition, divine gift, asceticism, and prophetic honor.

After defining the intellect broadly, the author enumerates five distinct types, each serving a different role: instinctive, acquired, granted by Allah, the intellect of the ascetics, and the ultimate prophetic intellect. This lesson breaks down each type and its significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the enumeration of the five types
Notice the order and the brief definition of each type.
2
Understand the instinctive and acquired types
The instinctive is the innate capacity for knowledge; the acquired comes through association with rational people.
3
Examine the divinely granted and ascetic types
Allah grants a special intellect to believers, and the intellect of the ascetics enables their renunciation.
4
Appreciate the prophetic intellect
The intellect of Prophet Muhammad is the most honorable, setting the highest standard.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والعَقْلُ كَالرُّوحِ مبتدأ وخبر؛ أي: والعقل مثل الروح من حيث الخوض في بيان الحقيقة والوقف عن ذلك، واختلف كلام المصنف في الترجيح : فرجح في «هداية المريد» طريق الخوض، ورجّح في «الكبير» طريق الوقف، وهو المختار؛ لأنه من المغيبات، وكلُّ ما هو كذلك فالأولى الكف عن الخوض فيه.
لغة: وهو المنع، من (عَقَلَ البعير) : إذا منعه بالعِقال، وسُمِّي بذلك لمنعه صاحبه من العدول عن سواء السبيل.
واعلم أن العقل على خمسة أنواع :
الأول: غريزي؛ وهو غريزة يُتَهيَّأ بها لدرك العلوم النظرية، كما قاله الإسلام.
والثاني : كسبي؛ وهو ما يكتسبه الإنسان من معاشرة العقلاء.
والثالث : عطائي؛ وهو ما يعطيه الله للمؤمن؛ ليهتدوا به إلى الإيمان.
والرابع: عقل الزهاد؛ وهو الذي يكون به الزهد.
والخامس شرفي؛ وهو عقل نبينا ﷺ؛ لأنه أشرف العقول.
His statement: (And the intellect is like the soul) is a subject and predicate; that is, the intellect is like the soul in terms of delving into the clarification of reality and refraining from that. The author's statement differed regarding the preponderance: he gave preponderance in 'Hidayat al-Murid' to the way of delving, and gave preponderance in 'al-Kabir' to the way of refraining, and that is the chosen view because it is among the hidden matters, and everything that is like that, the better course is to refrain from delving into it.
Linguistically: it is prevention, from 'he hobbled the camel' when he prevented it with the hobble; it is so named because it prevents its possessor from deviating from the straight path.
And know that the intellect is of five types:
First: instinctive (gharizi); it is an instinct by which one is prepared to grasp theoretical sciences, as Islam stated.
Second: acquired (kasbi); it is what a person acquires from associating with rational people.
Third: granted (ata'i); it is what Allah gives to the believer so that they may be guided thereby to faith.
Fourth: the intellect of the ascetics; it is that by which asceticism is achieved.
Fifth: honorary (sharafi); it is the intellect of our Prophet ﷺ, because it is the most honorable of intellects.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification. It begins by explaining the line 'And the intellect is like the soul'—meaning they are similar regarding whether to investigate their reality or refrain. The commentator notes that the author himself gave two different preponderances: in his earlier work 'Hidayat al-Murid' he favored investigation, but in 'al-Kabir' he favored refraining, and the latter is chosen because the intellect (like the soul) pertains to hidden matters (al-mughayyabat), so it is better to avoid delving into it. Then a linguistic definition is given: 'aql derives from 'aqala al-ba'ir' (to hobble a camel), and is so called because it prevents its possessor from deviating from the straight path. Finally, five types of intellect are enumerated: instinctive (gharizi) enabling theoretical knowledge, acquired (kasbi) through association, granted (ata'i) by Allah to believers, the intellect of ascetics (zuhhad) enabling asceticism, and the honorary (sharafi) intellect of the Prophet Muhammad ﷺ, being the most honorable. Each type is briefly explained.

Key Terms
غريزي (gharizi)
كسبي (kasbi)
عطائي (ata'i)
عقل الزهاد ('aql al-zuhhad)
شرفي (sharafi)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Intellect is only an innate rational faculty.
Correction: The text shows intellect can be acquired, divinely granted, and includes ascetic and prophetic dimensions.

Checkpoint
Which type of intellect is described as being given by Allah to guide believers to faith?
A) Instinctive
B) Acquired
C) Granted
D) Honorary

Key Takeaway
Intellect manifests in five forms: innate capacity, social learning, divine guidance, ascetic insight, and prophetic perfection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which of these five types of intellect is most lacking in your life right now? What one step can you take today to develop it?
?
Do you truly believe that Allah can grant you a special intellect ('aql 'ata'i) to guide you to faith, or have you been relying solely on your own reasoning? How would your life change if you actively sought that divine gift?
?
The Prophet's intellect is called the most honorable—are you connecting to that intellect by sincerely following his sunnah and seeking his intercession, or are you content with lesser forms of intellect?

What Is Kalam?
beginner
5 min
Disagreement on the Reality and Definitions of Intellect
The author explains the disagreement on the intellect and gives various scholarly definitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that scholars disagreed on the exact definition of the intellect, but all Ahl al-Sunnah agree it is an accident, and you will learn three specific definitions.

Core Idea
The intellect is an accident, but its precise definition varies among scholars.

In this passage, the commentator addresses a point of dispute: the exact nature of the human intellect. While scholars differ in their definitions, they all agree that it is an accident. This lesson unpacks that disagreement and the key definitions.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Disagreement
Read the opening lines about the corrective 'but' and the fact that scholars established disagreement concerning the intellect. Notice how the commentator clarifies the function of this phrase.
The passage suggests that disagreement about the intellect was widespread.
2
Identify the Consensus
Look for the statement that Ahl al-Sunnah are in agreement that the intellect is an accident ('arad). This is the foundational point.
Even though they differ on the definition, they all agree it is an accident, not a substance.
3
Learn the Three Definitions
Examine each definition: (1) knowledge of necessary sciences, (2) an instinct that leads to necessary knowledge, (3) an attribute that distinguishes good from evil. Note the scholars associated with each.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ولَكِنْ قَرَّرُوا فِيْهِ خِلَافاً أي لكن قرر العلماء في العقل خلافاً، ولا محل لهذا الاستدراك؛ لأنهم قرروا في الروح خلافاً أيضاً، فلعل (لكن) لمجرد التأكيد، ثم رأيت المصنف في شرحه قال: (ولكن ... إلى آخره) استدراك على طريقة الخائضين، فأشار إلى أنهم لم يتفقوا على حقيقةٍ معينةٍ، بل اختلفوا في بيانها. انتهى. فالاستدراك يُشعر بانتشار الخلاف وكثرته.
وقوله : (فَانْظُرَتْ ما فَسَّرُوا ) أي : فانظرن التفاسير التي ذكرها القوم في كتبهم، هذه المقدمة؛ لصغر حجمها. وأقوال أهل السنة متطابقة على عرضيته، فبعضهم قال: إنه من قبيل العلوم، وعرفه بأنه العلم ببعض العلوم الضرورية، كالعلم بوجوب تحيز الجرم، واستحالة عروه عن الحركة والسكون وجواز إحراق النار وغير ذلك، وهذا القول لإمام الحرمين وجماعة وبعضهم قال: (إنه ليس من قبيل العلوم، وعرفه بأنه غريزة؛ أي: طبيعة مغروزة يتبعها العلم بالضروريات عند سلامة الآلات)
وعرّفه الشيرازي بأنه صفةٌ يُميَّز بها بين الحسن والقبيح.
His statement: 'But they established disagreement concerning it'—meaning the scholars established disagreement concerning the intellect. There is no place for this correction because they also established disagreement concerning the soul. So perhaps 'but' is merely for emphasis. Then I saw that the author in his commentary said: ('But... etc.') is a correction to the method of those who delve (into hidden matters), indicating that they did not agree on a specific reality but differed in its explanation. End. So the correction suggests the spread and abundance of disagreement.
And his statement: 'So look at what they interpreted'—meaning look at the interpretations that the people mentioned in their books, this introduction because of its small size. And the statements of Ahl al-Sunnah are in agreement that it is an accident ('arad). Some said it belongs to the category of sciences, defining it as knowledge of some necessary sciences, such as the knowledge of the necessity of a body occupying space, the impossibility of it being devoid of motion and rest, the permissibility of fire burning, and other things. This is the statement of Imam al-Haramayn and a group. And some said: (It is not of the category of sciences, and defined it as an instinct; i.e., an ingrained nature that is followed by knowledge of necessities when the faculties are sound.)
And al-Shirazi defined it as an attribute by which one distinguishes between good and evil.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of two parts of the matn: 'but they established disagreement concerning it' and 'so look at what they interpreted'. First, the commentator notes that the word 'but' (lākin) appears as a correction to the method of those who delve into hidden matters, indicating that scholars did not agree on a single definition of the intellect but rather differed. He notes that there was also disagreement about the soul, so the 'but' may be for emphasis. Then, under 'so look at what they interpreted', the commentator urges the reader to examine the various interpretations given by scholars. He then presents the consensus of Ahl al-Sunnah that the intellect is an accident ('arad). He gives three specific definitions: 1) Some (like Imam al-Haramayn) define it as knowledge of necessary sciences (e.g., that bodies occupy space, cannot be devoid of motion/rest, fire burns). 2) Others define it as an instinct (gharizah) that leads to necessary knowledge when the senses are sound. 3) Al-Shirazi defines it as a faculty that distinguishes good from evil. The passage thus highlights the diversity of opinion on the exact nature of the intellect while affirming its accidental character.

Key Terms
العقل (al-'aql)
العرض (al-'arad)
العلوم الضرورية (al-'ulum al-daruriyyah)
غريزة (gharizah)
صفة (sifah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the intellect is a substance (jawhar).
Correction: Ahl al-Sunnah consensus is that it is an accident.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the consensus of Ahl al-Sunnah regarding the intellect?
A) It is a substance.
B) It is an accident.
C) It is a body.
D) It is a divine attribute.

Key Takeaway
The intellect is an accident according to Ahl al-Sunnah, but scholars offer varying definitions: as knowledge of necessary sciences, as an instinct, or as a distinguishing attribute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson reveals that even scholars debated the exact definition of the intellect. How often do you simply assume your intellect is correct without examining its foundation? Today, identify one belief you hold that you consider 'obvious' and ask yourself: is it based on necessary knowledge or just habit? What will you do to verify it?
?
The intellect is said to distinguish good from evil. In the next hour, before you make a decision—however small—pause and consciously use your intellect to judge whether the action is good or evil. Are you willing to do that, or do you prefer to follow impulse? Why?
